Return an empty ErrorList if there\n        are none.\n        \"\"\"\n        return self.errors.get(\n            NON_FIELD_ERRORS,\n            self.error_class(error_class=\"nonfield\", renderer=self.renderer),\n        )\n\n    def add_error(self, field, error):\n        \"\"\"\n        Update the content of `self._errors`.\n\n        The `field` argument is the name of the field to which the errors\n        should be added. If it's None, treat the errors as NON_FIELD_ERRORS.\n\n        The `error` argument can be a single error, a list of errors, or a\n        dictionary that maps field names to lists of errors. An \"error\" can be\n        either a simple string or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        message attribute set and a \"list or dictionary\" can be an actual\n        `list` or `dict` or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        `error_list` or `error_dict` attribute set.\n\n        If `error` is a dictionary, the `field` argument *must* be None and\n        errors will be added to the fields that correspond to the keys of the\n        dictionary.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not isinstance(error, ValidationError):\n            # Normalize to ValidationError and let its constructor\n            # do the hard work of making sense of the input.\n            error = ValidationError(error)\n\n        if hasattr(error, \"error_dict\"):\n            if field is not None:\n                raise TypeError(\n                    \"The argument `field` must be `None` when the `error` \"\n                    \"argument is a dictionary.\"\n                )\n            else:\n                error = error.error_dict\n        else:\n            error = {field or NON_FIELD_ERRORS: error.error_list}\n\n        for field, error_list in error.items():\n            if field not in self.errors:\n                if field != NON_FIELD_ERRORS and field not in self.fields:\n                    raise ValueError(\n                        \"'%s' has no field named '%s'.\"\n                        % (self.__class__.__name__, field)\n                    )\n                if field == NON_FIELD_ERRORS:\n                    self._errors[field] = self.error_class(\n                        error_class=\"nonfield\", renderer=self.renderer\n                    )\n                else:\n                    self._errors[field] = self.error_class(\n                        renderer=self.renderer,\n                        field_id=self[field].auto_id,\n                    )\n            self._errors[field].extend(error_list)\n            if field in self.cleaned_data:\n                del self.cleaned_data[field]\n\n    def has_error(self, field, code=None):\n        return field in self.errors and (\n            code is None\n            or any(error.code == code for error in self.errors.as_data()[field])\n        )\n\n    def full_clean(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Clean all of self.data and populate self._errors and self.cleaned_data.\n        \"\"\"\n        self._errors = ErrorDict(renderer=self.renderer)\n        if not self.is_bound:  # Stop further processing.\n            return\n        self.cleaned_data = {}\n        # If the form is permitted to be empty, and none of the form data has\n        # changed from the initial data, short circuit any validation.\n        if self.empty_permitted and not self.has_changed():\n            return\n\n        self._clean_fields()\n        self._clean_form()\n        self._post_clean()\n\n    def _clean_fields(self):\n        for name, bf in self._bound_items():\n            field = bf.field\n            try:\n                self.cleaned_data[name] = field._clean_bound_field(bf)\n                if hasattr(self, \"clean_%s\" % name):\n                    value = getattr(self, \"clean_%s\" % name)()\n                    self.cleaned_data[name] = value\n            except ValidationError as e:\n                self.add_error(name, e)\n\n    def _clean_form(self):\n        try:\n            cleaned_data = self.clean()\n        except ValidationError as e:\n            self.add_error(None, e)\n        else:\n            if cleaned_data is not None:\n                self.cleaned_data = cleaned_data\n\n    def _post_clean(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        An internal hook for performing additional cleaning after form cleaning\n        is complete. Used for model validation in model forms.\n        \"\"\"\n        pass\n\n    def clean(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Hook for doing any extra form-wide cleaning after Field.clean() has\n        been called on every field. Any ValidationError raised by this method\n        will not be associated with a particular field; it will have a\n        special-case association with the field named '__all__'.\n        \"\"\"\n        return self.cleaned_data\n\n    def has_changed(self):\n        \"\"\"Return True if data differs from initial.\"\"\"\n        return bool(self.changed_data)\n\n    @cached_property\n    def changed_data(self):\n        return [name for name, bf in self._bound_items() if bf._has_changed()]\n\n    @property\n    def media(self):\n        \"\"\"Return all media required to render the widgets on this form.\"\"\"\n        media = Media()\n        for field in self.fields.values():\n            media += field.widget.media\n        return media\n\n    def is_multipart(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return True if the form needs to be multipart-encoded, i.e. it has\n        FileInput, or False otherwise.\n        \"\"\"\n        return any(field.widget.needs_multipart_form for field in self.fields.values())\n\n    def hidden_fields(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return a list of all the BoundField objects that are hidden fields.\n        Useful for manual form layout in templates.\n        \"\"\"\n        return [field for field in self if field.is_hidden]\n\n    def visible_fields(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return a list of BoundField objects that aren't hidden fields.\n        The opposite of the hidden_fields() method.\n        \"\"\"\n        return [field for field in self if not field.is_hidden]\n\n    def get_initial_for_field(self, field, field_name):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return initial data for field on form. Use initial data from the form\n        or the field, in that order. Evaluate callable values.\n        \"\"\"\n        value = self.initial.get(field_name, field.initial)\n        if callable(value):\n            value = value()\n        # If this is an auto-generated default date, nix the microseconds\n        # for standardized handling. See #22502.\n        if (\n            isinstance(value, (datetime.datetime, datetime.time))\n            and not field.widget.supports_microseconds\n        ):\n            value = value.replace(microsecond=0)\n        return value\n\n\nclass Form(BaseForm, metaclass=DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass):\n    \"A collection of Fields, plus their associated data.\"\n\n    # This is a separate class from BaseForm in order to abstract the way\n    # self.fields is specified. This class (Form) is the one that does the\n    # fancy metaclass stuff purely for the semantic sugar -- it allows one\n    # to define a form using declarative syntax.\n    # BaseForm itself has no way of designating self.fields.\n","numLines":440,"startLine":1,"totalLines":440}}}

If it's None, treat the errors as NON_FIELD_ERRORS.\n\n        The `error` argument can be a single error, a list of errors, or a\n        dictionary that maps field names to lists of errors. An \"error\" can be\n        either a simple string or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        message attribute set and a \"list or dictionary\" can be an actual\n        `list` or `dict` or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        `error_list` or `error_dict` attribute set.\n\n        If `error` is a dictionary, the `field` argument *must* be None and\n        errors will be added to the fields that correspond to the keys of the\n        dictionary.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not isinstance(error, ValidationError):\n            # An \"error\" can be\n        either a simple string or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        message attribute set and a \"list or dictionary\" can be an actual\n        `list` or `dict` or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        `error_list` or `error_dict` attribute set.\n\n        If `error` is a dictionary, the `field` argument *must* be None and\n        errors will be added to the fields that correspond to the keys of the\n        dictionary.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not isinstance(error, ValidationError):\n            # Because a particular *instance* of the class might want to\n        # alter self.fields, we create self.fields here by copying base_fields.\n        # Instances should always modify self.fields; they should not modify\n        # self.base_fields.\n        self.fields = copy.deepcopy(self.base_fields)\n        self._bound_fields_cache = {}\n        self.order_fields(self.field_order if field_order is None else field_order)\n\n        if use_required_attribute is not None:\n            self.use_required_attribute = use_required_attribute\n\n        if self.empty_permitted and self.use_required_attribute:\n            raise ValueError(\n                \"The empty_permitted and use_required_attribute arguments may \"\n                \"not both be True.\"\n            )\n\n        # Initialize form renderer. Use a global default if not specified\n        # either as an argument or as self.default_renderer.\n        if renderer is None:\n            if self.default_renderer is None:\n                renderer = get_default_renderer()\n            else:\n                renderer = self.default_renderer\n                if isinstance(self.default_renderer, type):\n                    renderer = renderer()\n        self.renderer = renderer\n\n        self.bound_field_class = (\n            bound_field_class\n            or self.bound_field_class\n            or getattr(self.renderer, \"bound_field_class\", None)\n        )\n\n    def order_fields(self, field_order):\n        \"\"\"\n        Rearrange the fields according to field_order.\n\n        field_order is a list of field names specifying the order. Append\n        fields not included in the list in the default order for backward\n        compatibility with subclasses not overriding field_order. If\n        field_order is None, keep all fields in the order defined in the class.\n        Ignore unknown fields in field_order to allow disabling fields in form\n        subclasses without redefining ordering.\n        \"\"\"\n        if field_order is None:\n            return\n        fields = {}\n        for key in field_order:\n            try:\n                fields[key] = self.fields.pop(key)\n            except KeyError:  # ignore unknown fields\n                pass\n        fields.update(self.fields)  # add remaining fields in original order\n        self.fields = fields\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        if self._errors is None:\n            is_valid = \"Unknown\"\n        else:\n            is_valid = self.is_bound and not self._errors\n        return \"<%(cls)s bound=%(bound)s, valid=%(valid)s, fields=(%(fields)s)>\" % {\n            \"cls\": self.__class__.__name__,\n            \"bound\": self.is_bound,\n            \"valid\": is_valid,\n            \"fields\": \";\".join(self.fields),\n        }\n\n    def _bound_items(self):\n        \"\"\"Yield (name, bf) pairs, where bf is a BoundField object.\"\"\"\n        for name in self.fields:\n            yield name, self[name]\n\n    def __iter__(self):\n        \"\"\"Yield the form's fields as BoundField objects.\"\"\"\n        for name in self.fields:\n            yield self[name]\n\n    def __getitem__(self, name):\n        \"\"\"Return a BoundField with the given name.\"\"\"\n        try:\n            field = self.fields[name]\n        except KeyError:\n            raise KeyError(\n                \"Key '%s' not found in '%s'. Choices are: %s.\"\n                % (\n                    name,\n                    self.__class__.__name__,\n                    \", \".join(sorted(self.fields)),\n                )\n            )\n        if name not in self._bound_fields_cache:\n            self._bound_fields_cache[name] = field.get_bound_field(self, name)\n        return self._bound_fields_cache[name]\n\n    @property\n    def errors(self):\n        \"\"\"Return an ErrorDict for the data provided for the form.\"\"\"\n        if self._errors is None:\n            self.full_clean()\n        return self._errors\n\n    def is_valid(self):\n        \"\"\"Return True if the form has no errors, or False otherwise.\"\"\"\n        return self.is_bound and not self.errors\n\n    def add_prefix(self, field_name):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return the field name with a prefix appended, if this Form has a\n        prefix set.\n\n        Subclasses may wish to override.\n        \"\"\"\n        return \"%s-%s\" % (self.prefix, field_name) if self.prefix else field_name\n\n    def add_initial_prefix(self, field_name):\n        \"\"\"Add an 'initial' prefix for checking dynamic initial values.\"\"\"\n        return \"initial-%s\" % self.add_prefix(field_name)\n\n    def _widget_data_value(self, widget, html_name):\n        # value_from_datadict() gets the data from the data dictionaries.\n        # Each widget type knows how to retrieve its own data, because some\n        # widgets split data over several HTML fields.\n        return widget.value_from_datadict(self.data, self.files, html_name)\n\n    @property\n    def template_name(self):\n        return self.renderer.form_template_name\n\n    def get_context(self):\n        fields = []\n        hidden_fields = []\n        top_errors = self.non_field_errors().copy()\n        for name, bf in self._bound_items():\n            if bf.is_hidden:\n                if bf.errors:\n                    top_errors += [\n                        _(\"(Hidden field %(name)s) %(error)s\")\n                        % {\"name\": name, \"error\": str(e)}\n                        for e in bf.errors\n                    ]\n                hidden_fields.append(bf)\n            else:\n                fields.append((bf, bf.errors))\n        return {\n            \"form\": self,\n            \"fields\": fields,\n            \"hidden_fields\": hidden_fields,\n            \"errors\": top_errors,\n        }\n\n    def non_field_errors(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return an ErrorList of errors that aren't associated with a particular\n        field -- i.e., from Form.clean(). Return an empty ErrorList if there\n        are none.\n        \"\"\"\n        return self.errors.get(\n            NON_FIELD_ERRORS,\n            self.error_class(error_class=\"nonfield\", renderer=self.renderer),\n        )\n\n    def add_error(self, field, error):\n        \"\"\"\n        Update the content of `self._errors`.\n\n        The `field` argument is the name of the field to which the errors\n        should be added. If it's None, treat the errors as NON_FIELD_ERRORS.\n\n        The `error` argument can be a single error, a list of errors, or a\n        dictionary that maps field names to lists of errors. An \"error\" can be\n        either a simple string or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        message attribute set and a \"list or dictionary\" can be an actual\n        `list` or `dict` or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        `error_list` or `error_dict` attribute set.\n\n        If `error` is a dictionary, the `field` argument *must* be None and\n        errors will be added to the fields that correspond to the keys of the\n        dictionary.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not isinstance(error, ValidationError):\n            # Used for model validation in model forms.\n        \"\"\"\n        pass\n\n    def clean(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Hook for doing any extra form-wide cleaning after Field.clean() has\n        been called on every field. Any ValidationError raised by this method\n        will not be associated with a particular field; it will have a\n        special-case association with the field named '__all__'.\n        \"\"\"\n        return self.cleaned_data\n\n    def has_changed(self):\n        \"\"\"Return True if data differs from initial.\"\"\"\n        return bool(self.changed_data)\n\n    @cached_property\n    def changed_data(self):\n        return [name for name, bf in self._bound_items() if bf._has_changed()]\n\n    @property\n    def media(self):\n        \"\"\"Return all media required to render the widgets on this form.\"\"\"\n        media = Media()\n        for field in self.fields.values():\n            media += field.widget.media\n        return media\n\n    def is_multipart(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return True if the form needs to be multipart-encoded, i.e. it has\n        FileInput, or False otherwise.\n        \"\"\"\n        return any(field.widget.needs_multipart_form for field in self.fields.values())\n\n    def hidden_fields(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return a list of all the BoundField objects that are hidden fields.\n        Useful for manual form layout in templates.\n        \"\"\"\n        return [field for field in self if field.is_hidden]\n\n    def visible_fields(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return a list of BoundField objects that aren't hidden fields.\n        The opposite of the hidden_fields() method.\n        \"\"\"\n        return [field for field in self if not field.is_hidden]\n\n    def get_initial_for_field(self, field, field_name):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return initial data for field on form. Use initial data from the form\n        or the field, in that order. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01MKfr3SCWHXF5dWmAhZYiwF","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_018BBEm9rs4VZBBTauxry8jn","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/COMPOSITE_VALIDATOR_EXAMPLE.md","content":"# CompositeFieldValidator Usage Guide\n\nThe `CompositeFieldValidator` class allows you to validate relationships between multiple form fields simultaneously. It integrates seamlessly with Django's existing form validation pipeline.\n\n## Basic Usage\n\n### Simple Date Range Validation\n\n```python\nfrom django import forms\n\ndef validate_date_range(start_date, end_date):\n    \"\"\"Validation function that returns True if validation passes.\"\"\"\n    if start_date and end_date:\n        return end_date > start_date\n    return True\n\nclass EventForm(forms.Form):\n    start_date = forms.DateField()\n    end_date = forms.DateField()\n\n    # Attach the composite validator as a class attribute\n    date_range_validator = forms.CompositeFieldValidator(\n        validation_function=validate_date_range,\n        field_names=['start_date', 'end_date'],\n        message='End date must be after start date.'\n    )\n```\n\n### Email Confirmation Validation\n\n```python\nclass RegistrationForm(forms.Form):\n    email = forms.EmailField()\n    email_confirm = forms.EmailField()\n\n    def validate_emails_match(email, email_confirm):\n        if email and email_confirm:\n            return email == email_confirm\n        return True\n\n    email_validator = forms.CompositeFieldValidator(\n        validation_function=validate_emails_match,\n        field_names=['email', 'email_confirm'],\n        message='Email addresses do not match.'\n    )\n```\n\n### Password Confirmation Validation\n\n```python\nclass PasswordChangeForm(forms.Form):\n    new_password = forms.CharField(widget=forms.PasswordInput)\n    confirm_password = forms.CharField(widget=forms.PasswordInput)\n\n    def passwords_match(new_password, confirm_password):\n        if new_password and confirm_password:\n            return new_password == confirm_password\n        return True\n\n    password_validator = forms.CompositeFieldValidator(\n        validation_function=passwords_match,\n        field_names=['new_password', 'confirm_password'],\n        message='Passwords do not match.'\n    )\n```\n\n## Advanced Usage\n\n### Multiple Validators on One Form\n\n```python\nclass ProductForm(forms.Form):\n    regular_price = forms.DecimalField()\n    sale_price = forms.DecimalField()\n    discount_percent = forms.IntegerField()\n\n    def validate_sale_price(regular_price, sale_price):\n        if regular_price and sale_price:\n            return sale_price < regular_price\n        return True\n\n    def validate_discount(regular_price, discount_percent):\n        if regular_price and discount_percent is not None:\n            return 0 < discount_percent < 100\n        return True\n\n    price_validator = forms.CompositeFieldValidator(\n        validation_function=validate_sale_price,\n        field_names=['regular_price', 'sale_price'],\n        message='Sale price must be less than regular price.'\n    )\n\n    discount_validator = forms.CompositeFieldValidator(\n        validation_function=validate_discount,\n        field_names=['regular_price', 'discount_percent'],\n        message='Discount must be between 0 and 100 percent.'\n    )\n```\n\n### Complex Validation with Multiple Fields\n\n```python\nclass RoomBookingForm(forms.Form):\n    check_in_date = forms.DateField()\n    check_out_date = forms.DateField()\n    num_adults = forms.IntegerField()\n    num_children = forms.IntegerField()\n\n    def validate_booking(check_in_date, check_out_date, num_adults, num_children):\n        # Check-out must be after check-in\n        if check_in_date and check_out_date:\n            if check_out_date <= check_in_date:\n                return False\n\n        # Must have at least one guest\n        total_guests = (num_adults or 0) + (num_children or 0)\n        if total_guests < 1:\n            return False\n\n        return True\n\n    booking_validator = forms.CompositeFieldValidator(\n        validation_function=validate_booking,\n        field_names=['check_in_date', 'check_out_date', 'num_adults', 'num_children'],\n        message='Invalid booking details. Ensure check-out is after check-in and at least one guest is specified.'\n    )\n```\n\n## How It Works\n\n1. **Declaration**: CompositeFieldValidator instances are declared as class attributes on form classes.\n\n2. **Collection**: Django's form metaclass collects these validators during class creation.\n\n3. **Initialization**: When a form instance is created, validators are copied from the class-level definitions.\n\n4. **Validation**: During form validation (when `is_valid()` is called):\n   - Individual field validation occurs first (`_clean_fields()`)\n   - Form-wide validation occurs next (`_clean_form()`)\n   - Composite validators are executed, passing the cleaned data\n   - Errors are added to the form's non-field errors\n\n5. **Error Handling**: When validation fails, the error message is added as a non-field error, appearing at the top of the form.\n\n## Key Features\n\n### Missing Field Handling\n\nIf a referenced field doesn't exist in the form or wasn't included in the submitted data, the validator gracefully skips validation:\n\n```python\n# If 'nonexistent_field' is missing, validation is skipped\nvalidator = forms.CompositeFieldValidator(\n    validation_function=some_func,\n    field_names=['existing_field', 'nonexistent_field'],\n    message='Validation error'\n)\n```\n\n### Validation Function Requirements\n\n- Accepts keyword arguments matching the field names\n- Returns `True` if validation passes, `False` if it fails\n- Should handle `None` values gracefully\n- Can access multiple field values to determine validity\n\n### Error Reporting\n\n- Errors are reported as non-field errors (appear at the top of the form)\n- Compatible with Django's form error display in templates\n- Uses Django's standard `ValidationError` class\n\n## Integration with Django's Validation Pipeline\n\nCompositeFieldValidator integrates into the existing form validation flow:\n\n```\nform.is_valid()\n    ↓\nfull_clean()\n    ↓\n_clean_fields()  ← Individual field validation\n    ↓\n_clean_form()    ← clean() method + CompositeFieldValidator runs here\n    ↓\n_post_clean()    ← Hook for model validation\n```\n\n## Example in Templates\n\nForms with composite validation errors display as:\n\n```html\n<form method=\"post\">\n    {% csrf_token %}\n\n    {# Non-field errors appear first #}\n    {% if form.non_field_errors %}\n        <div class=\"errors\">\n            {% for error in form.non_field_errors %}\n                <p class=\"error\">{{ error }}</p>\n            {% endfor %}\n        </div>\n    {% endif %}\n\n    {# Then field-specific errors #}\n    {{ form.start_date }}\n    {{ form.end_date }}\n\n    <button type=\"submit\">Submit</button>\n</form>\n```\n\n## Best Practices\n\n1. **Clear validation functions**: Make validator functions readable and well-documented\n2. **Meaningful error messages**: Use specific messages that help users correct errors\n3. **Handle edge cases**: Return `True` for None values to allow optional fields\n4. **Descriptive names**: Use clear names for validator attributes on the form\n5. **Keep it simple**: For very complex validation, consider overriding the `clean()` method instead\n\n## Comparison with clean() Method Override\n\n### Using CompositeFieldValidator (Recommended)\n```python\nclass MyForm(forms.Form):\n    field1 = forms.CharField()\n    field2 = forms.CharField()\n\n    validator = forms.CompositeFieldValidator(\n        validation_function=lambda field1, field2: field1 != field2,\n        field_names=['field1', 'field2'],\n        message='Fields must be different.'\n    )\n```\n\n### Using clean() Override (Alternative)\n```python\nclass MyForm(forms.Form):\n    field1 = forms.CharField()\n    field2 = forms.CharField()\n\n    def clean(self):\n        cleaned_data = super().clean()\n        if cleaned_data.get('field1') == cleaned_data.get('field2'):\n            raise forms.ValidationError('Fields must be different.')\n        return cleaned_data\n```\n\nThe CompositeFieldValidator approach is cleaner and more maintainable for simple cross-field validations.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":0,"cache_creation_input_tokens":758,"cache_read_input_tokens":69548,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":758},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"f2f3046f-30a6-4594-aeff-3c2bbcf569c7","uuid":"16ba396d-2805-4d75-8f76-186a5ffe85b7"}
